Shen Bao Amateur Weekly

Amateur Musings

What is the Significance of Anglo-French Cooperation? 317

— Yu Ming

Not long ago, the diplomatic authorities of Britain and France clashed head-on over the issue of "security guarantees" in Geneva, causing the disarmament conference to virtually stall and the European situation to become frozen. Shortly thereafter, French Foreign Minister Barthou suddenly visited London, and immediately the news of Anglo-French cooperation was released. Consequently, Britain and Italy agreed to the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact, and the Soviet Union will join the League of Nations within two weeks. The changes in the European situation have become a major issue in current international politics.

We know that politicians in London have always disliked any country vying with them for hegemony in Europe. Before the European War, because of Germany's expanding power, which threatened Britain's position as leader everywhere, Britain had to ally with France and Russia to counter the rising Germany. After the war, Germany's armed forces were disarmed, its colonies were seized, and it had lost the ability to compete with Britain for hegemony. At the same time, on the other hand, France, with the Versailles system, eyed Europe covetously. The expansion of its army, navy, and air force, the increase in its economic power, and the rise of its political status all made the British Empire feel uneasy. Therefore, "boosting Germany and suppressing France" became the center of Britain's post-war foreign policy in Europe. Recently, due to Franco-Soviet amity, German-Polish cooperation, the alliance between Italy, Austria, and Hungary, and the meeting between the French and Italian prime ministers in Venice, the tangled diplomatic policies and collusive relationships among European countries have become concretely evident. Under these circumstances, if Franco-Soviet relations become increasingly friendly, and the small countries of the Baltic and Balkan regions further protect them, London would naturally feel uneasy. At the same time, the closeness between Italy and Germany has the potential to develop into the realization of a Central European alliance, which also poses a threat to Britain. Moreover, Italy's recent expansion of its navy and construction of warships is something that Britain, which prides itself on being the master of the seas, can hardly sit idly by and watch. Therefore, in order to ease Anglo-French conflict and prevent various possible crises, London's diplomats have had to superficially change their past foreign policy. Thus, Barthou's trip to London was not in vain, and temporary Anglo-French cooperation became a reality.

However, to say that Britain and France have completely understood each other from now on, and that the European situation has moved towards peace, is still inconsistent with objective facts. The main manifestation of the so-called Anglo-French cooperation is Britain's recognition of France's security guarantee plan and its support for the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact, which is not enough to say that Britain and France have reached complete understanding in all aspects. Moreover, France's security guarantee plan, the so-called Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact, is actually aimed at preventing Germany. However, London is linking German military equality with security guarantees, meaning that on the one hand, it supports the Paris plan to make Germany comply to a certain extent and return to Geneva in order to ease Anglo-French conflict, and on the other hand, it supports Germany's rearmament to counter France. At the same time, Italy, which is changing its attitude along with Britain, has more specifically stated: "Italy does not oppose the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact for three reasons: (1) Italy is certain that this pact is not directed against Germany; (2) Italy believes that this pact recognizes Germany's right to military equality; (3) ......" From this, it can be seen that even on the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact, Britain, France, Italy, and other countries all have their own hidden agendas, and their opinions are not unified. Recently, a section of the French press has expressed great dissatisfaction with British Foreign Secretary Simon's remarks, even declaring that they "felt as if they had a nightmare" after hearing Simon's remarks. At the same time, Barthou also formally stated: "If anyone asks me to provide the conditions for establishing the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact after hearing Simon's remarks, then I cannot agree." This is the beginning of the expression of Anglo-French differences. Therefore, we can say that Britain and France have reached a temporary agreement on the surface, but it would be a mistake to say that they have completely understood each other, let alone that the European situation has moved towards peace.

As for the fundamental contradictions between Germany and France, France and Italy, Germany, Austria, and Italy, and even Britain and France, they have not only not been resolved, but are also developing. The ultimate solution to these contradictions is war. Before the outbreak of war, that is, before the imperialist powers are fully prepared for war, they have no choice but to use various methods to ease their real contradictions in order to practically prepare for war. The significance of the so-called Anglo-French cooperation, and even Franco-Italian understanding, is nothing more than this. In the future, the development path of Europe and even the world may be very tortuous on the surface, but it must have a general goal, which is to move towards war. This is what we can assert.

Life

Under the Mercury Lamp 318

— Youqun

The lives of movie stars, as depicted in today's newspapers and magazines, often touch only on the surface of luxury and happiness. The underlying layers of hard work and tears hidden behind those words are often missed by the clever pens of those contributors. In reality, it's difficult to indulge in luxurious and happy dreams in the movie circle. Those who make a living under the mercury lamp are definitely not a group of happy people. The lives of movie stars are definitely not as ideal and beautiful as many people imagine. They are just puppets of labor, like employees in other industrial sectors.

Despite the fact that some people see becoming a star as their greatest fantasy, the reality under the mercury lamp shatters their daydreams. Here, I must first point out that this is not an ideal occupation. We may as well start with the aspect of treatment. Everyone knows how surprisingly disparate the treatment of stars is. For example, in China, the most popular actress can earn about 20,000 yuan a year, while the monthly income of a well-known actor rarely exceeds 300 yuan. It is not surprising for an ordinary actress with some fame to receive 300, 400, 500, or 600 yuan per month from the company. No matter how much the boss promotes him, it is very difficult for such an actor to get more than 200 yuan from the boss's pocket. No matter how much acting talent you have, even if your talent is sufficient to play the leading role in the film and you have been assigned to play the leading role, it is difficult for you to earn more than 30 yuan per month as a male actor who is new to the screen. This kind of unfair treatment of these "new" stars often causes an inexplicable indignation in the person concerned. They must constantly be thinking of ways to get rid of this cage. But on the one hand, the harsh reality of life makes them have to work hard to maintain this "position", and wish they could sign longer-term contracts with the bosses. Can we say anything to blame this contradiction in life?

This unequal treatment has opened up a road for film companies to find new talents. In order to guarantee the future success of their business, the bosses are willing to pay more to poach those who are frustrated with their meager salaries from their business competitors. Their generosity and generosity are sometimes astonishing. They are willing to increase the salaries of their employees by double or more than two-thirds. Some people who have played leading roles may only receive 60 yuan per month in their original company, but another company will buy his (or her) labor for 100 yuan a month, and yet another company will even use 120 yuan to ask him or her to help out. (This is just an example. The salaries of more famous stars are even higher. She may only get more than 200 yuan per month in the original company, but another company may hire her for 300 or 400 yuan.) Of course, those who have the qualifications to be snatched up by others are unwilling to sign long-term contracts with the bosses. A one-year contract is considered the most suitable for them or her.

Small Monographs

Discussing China's Current Grain Problem from the Soaring Price of Rice 319

— Katayama

For the past month, due to the drought, not only have the old farmers felt all kinds of hardships, but also the small and medium-sized bourgeoisie in the cities have similarly recognized a huge crisis. Let's not talk about anything else, but just take the most important food problem in our "clothing, food, housing", half a month ago, the top grade white rice was only worth 9.2 yuan per bag, but recently (15th), its price has soared to 12.8 yuan; in just half a month, it has risen by 5.6 yuan in a row.

Those who eat top-grade white rice are mostly the relatively wealthy class. Our working friends are very lucky if they can eat second-grade white rice or Pinghu white japonica rice: but even the lowest Pinghu rice has risen from 8.2 yuan on June 28 to 10.6 yuan on the 15th. Under such circumstances, coupled with the harsh weather, it is as the newspaper said recently: "The common people cannot live."

The soaring price of rice is a fact, and the manipulation of merchants is also a fact; but these facts are only temporary phenomena. Outside of this temporary phenomenon, there is a fundamental problem. Now let's talk about this fundamental problem.

China is an ancient country that is based on agriculture. Before the sea ban was lifted, although it sometimes had to rely slightly on Siam, Taiwan, and other places due to natural disasters, in general, it was still able to be self-sufficient: but since the Republic of China, this "self-sufficiency" has gradually been broken. Domestic rice is increasingly insufficient for self-use, while foreign rice is flowing in like a tide. Regarding the situation of foreign rice imports, please see the following table:

Republic of China Year 1: 2,700,493 Dan

Republic of China Year 5: 11,284,025

Republic of China Year 10: 10,634,560

Republic of China Year 15: 18,720,777

Republic of China Year 20: 10,740,810

Republic of China Year 23: 21,423,091

Look, an annual leakage of 20 million dan and a deficit of 150 million yuan. In a country that is based on agriculture, this phenomenon is appalling!

However, please do not sigh at this number: now let's investigate the reasons for this matter.

Everyone knows that when the imperialists used machine guns and cannons to conquer colonies or semi-colonies, what followed was economic aggression, which was based on the principle of absorbing the latter's raw materials and selling their own manufactured goods. However, when this kind of aggression reached a certain stage, because it destroyed all the economic foundations of the semi-colony, the latter not only needed the supply of manufactured goods from imperialism, but also had to rely on others for raw materials. China's current food problem is the most obvious example of this phenomenon.

In recent years, although the government has taken measures to increase the import tax on foreign rice, as a result of (1) the poor rice production in our country recently, (2) the inconvenience of transportation, and (3) the failure to abolish exorbitant taxes, the price of rice has instead been raised step by step.

This gradual upward trend is actually only deliberately manipulated by merchants and is of no benefit to the old farmers. Recently, rice merchants have used the drought as an excuse to raise the price of rice by one-half in just half a month, which is a very serious problem for people's food!

Under such circumstances, it is absolutely not enough to simply increase import taxes. Only by further actively increasing rice production, developing transportation, earnestly abolishing exorbitant taxes, and strictly cracking down on merchants' speculation and manipulation can we relieve our current disaster!

Regarding contracts, I might as well say a few more words. Those who hope to sign long-term contracts are mostly actors who are new to the screen. They are content to allow the company boss to have full control over the freedom of their bodies for a uniform price of 20 yuan, 30 yuan, or at most 50 yuan per month for three or five years. They or she initially thought that this was a not a small sum, and were fortunate that their own and their families' lives were guaranteed; who knows, most of those who sell their labor at such a low price are very intelligent and talented people (especially female stars). Once they appear on the screen and meet the audience, they will immediately cause a sensation and be recognized as a bright star, but her or his salary is still at the level of an unknown person. She or he never expected to have such a lucky day. She or he may feel remorse in her heart for the previous excessive concern for life security. Now that the boss has filled his pockets because of her or him, she or he is embarrassed not to take out a small part of the profit and automatically increase her or his salary by 20 or 30 yuan per month, or distribute this money as "reward money" to those who are not very successful but have talent.

What I said above refers to the official or "basic" actors of each company. In addition, there is an actor who does have certain talents and is suitable for the role of a certain special person in a certain script, but he is not necessarily suitable for the general needs of a certain company. In this way, he can only be hired by the boss for a short period of time. This is the so-called "guest" actor. Most of the "guest" actors have the contract stipulating the filming of a certain designated play. The minimum reward for "guest" acting in a play will not be less than 100; 150 yuan and 200 yuan are also available. However, it is rare to see 300 yuan for a play. The minimum time for filming a play will never be less than one or two months. It is not considered long to be three or four months in general, and it is not uncommon to be six or seven months, or eight or nine months.

In addition to the guest actors, there is also a kind of extra. Most of the extras are hired as "moving scenery". There are not many shots, and the position is not important, but they are indispensable. For example, art cannot be without an audience (many musicians are also often hired as extras), a church cannot be without prostitutes, and a factory cannot be without female workers ... Thus, a large number of extras are very necessary. Usually, the price of hard work for an extra for a day is one dollar, and some days you can earn a little more than one dollar. If there are dramas to be filmed every day, you can earn up to 40 yuan per month, which is more considerable than the income of a "new" or "　　" actor. (The monthly salary of a basic actor in a large movie company in Shanghai is only seven yuan!) But there are very, very few people who have such good luck.

Some of the extras are unemployed film workers, ordinary unemployed people, and hired prostitutes; some are people who rely on the position of "extra" to eat. There are also some curious gentlemen and ladies who take pleasure and pride in appearing on the screen and occasionally come out to show off in front of the audience.

The reason for the disparity in treatment of actors as mentioned above is said to be due to the difference in talent (?) and experience; but in the movie industry, there are people with insufficient talent and little experience who are also acting as gardeners. There is a kind of actor who specializes in using certain characteristics or defects on his body to eat. For example, Laurel and Hardy rely on their fat and thinness, and Buster Keaton relies on his "cold face", etc. Some Chinese film companies like to raise fat people, so "selling meat" has also become a profession. No matter how inconvenient obesity makes people move, but for a salary of 40 or 50 yuan a month, fat people have to eat more "pig brains", and make their bodies more dull, so as to win the audience's smile. There are also people who use their defects such as "squinting eyes" to appear in the so-called "gimmick" interlude shots to amuse the audience ... In short, there is nothing strange in the film industry, and I don’t have time to talk about it in detail here.

Now I want to talk about the stars'

Page 21

personal lives. Even a famous star cannot avoid often complaining about being poor. Most of their qualifications are only suitable for living in the more beautiful apartments in the area of ​​Xuhui District, and the suits are made for them by the stores in the area of ​​Wusong Road. In terms of meals, they may be regular customers of Russian restaurants, or they may also be in the humble position of a cook with the qualifications of a big star (naturally it cannot be generalized). What they are most heartbroken about is probably the company’s arrears of wages for several months in a row. The company sometimes decides the number of salaries based on whether a certain film is "popular" or not. If that film happens to be very "unpopular", then they are really unlucky. They will feel panic in all aspects.

However, some stars still have to waste their limited income. You can find them living a decadent life in the corners of the dance hall. Also, because of the liberation of men and women and the frequency of contact, a pair of lovers will be created at super speed. From this, pairs of people go to dance halls, swimming pools, movie theaters, cafes ... are all very ordinary.

Because of considerable waste, they have to dream of getting rich. In terms of their current situation, it is absolutely difficult for them to become "rich" like American stars, so some people harbor improper intentions, either buying aviation lottery tickets or buying champagne tickets for racecourses or Jai Alai courts, in order to get something for nothing. In order to "become famous", some people's "climbing the dragon" does not hesitate to go in the direction of depravity and crime. The rape cases of movie stars are not just seen once or twice.

In order to get the praise and promotion of bosses, directors, and people in the film industry, flattery and contribution of everything they own (female stars) is often a necessary means. Therefore, some self-respecting stars would rather jump out of this dark film circle and not be willing to go with the flow.

Finally, I want to point out that although many stars seem to live a luxurious life on the surface, they are not necessarily truly happy people. Ai Xia's suicide is a good example.

Sunday Literary Society

Mr. Liu Fu and the Chinese New Literature Movement 320

— Shao Wen

According to reports, the literary figure Liu Fu passed away at 2:10 PM on the 14th of this month in Beiping. The news has been met with deep sorrow in academic circles. Furthermore, mourning articles by Mr. Shou Tonghe and Mr. Chen Zizhan have already appeared in the "Free Talk" section of this newspaper, offering a fair assessment of Mr. Liu's efforts in linguistics and his personal character. Now, in mourning for Mr. Liu, I specifically recount his relationship with the Chinese New Literature Movement, hoping to evoke a shared sentiment among everyone.

Mr. Liu Funong was one of the main figures in the May Fourth Literary Revolution. At that time, Mr. Liu's opposition to the old classical Chinese and his advocacy for the new vernacular literature were, in many respects, even more proactive than those of Mr. Hu Shi. The revolutionary spirit expressed in his "My Views on Literary Reform" (published in "New Youth," Vol. 3, No. 3) can be considered a step further than Mr. Hu Shi's "Eight No's." This can be seen in his words: "…The term 'eliminate superstition' seems similar to Mr. Hu's two items of 'not imitating the ancients,' but it is actually a step further than Mr. Hu. Mr. Hu only says that the writings of the ancients should not be imitated, but I say that unless the dead form of ancient writing is overturned, the new literature will never be able to break away from the old literature's conventions. Most of the essays written by people today rigidly adhere to the four characters of 'beginning, development, turn, and conclusion,' which are as unbreakable as the 'tortoise head' and 'butterfly clip' terms of the eight-legged essay writers… If we want to build the foundation of a new literature, we must first break this superstition of worshiping the old literary forms, so that literature can quickly display a new brilliance in form…" As for how to reform prose and verse and how to resolve formal issues, Mr. Liu had very progressive opinions in this article.

Mr. Liu had a particular interest in poetry. In his article "Innovation in the Spirit of Poetry and Fiction" (published in "New Youth," Vol. 3, No. 5), he said: "The original intention of writing poetry is simply to express the truest point in one's thoughts using natural sounds and rhythms, and that is considered excellent." Such a correct view is probably something that those poets who only talk about flowers and the moon and do not pay attention to the "true" content of their thoughts will never understand. However, Mr. Liu expressed this as early as the May Fourth era, which cannot help but make us admire him. As for his attack on Confucianism in this article, it demonstrated an exceptionally bold spirit. He publicly declared that Confucius, who had been revered as a sage by the Chinese people for thousands of years, committed a heinous crime by abridging the "Book of Songs," saying that Confucius was "simply the greatest criminal in Chinese literature!"

At the same time, Mr. Liu not only made brilliant contributions to the theory of the New Literature Movement but also used vernacular language to create many new poems to counter classical Chinese writing. We can say that he was a theorist, a critic, and also a creator, a poet. His poems such as "Separated by a Layer of Paper" and "The Apprentice's Suffering" were all completed with a new consciousness and a new form. At that time, although Mr. Hu Shi and Mr. Shen Yinmo also wrote poems in vernacular Chinese, they were all confined by the form of old poetry, not daring to break the old rules and write poems in the form of prose. However, in "New Youth," Vol. 4, No. 5, Mr. Liu Fu began to experiment with "unrhymed poetry," and his "Selling Radishes" was one of the earliest "unrhymed poems" to appear in China.

Of course, Mr. Liu's poems not only had many shortcomings in form, but also were full of humanistic consciousness in content; from the current point of view, this is, of course, considered backward. However, under the general cultural level at that time, in such an enlightenment movement, I think it is still rare that Mr. Liu was able to create such works.

Just as the May Fourth Literary Revolution was not thorough, it goes without saying that there were also many non-thorough opinions in Mr. Liu's views on the New Literature Movement. But this responsibility cannot be entirely borne by Mr. Liu; the main person responsible should be Chinese society. Because under the social conditions of China at that time, only such a literary revolution could be produced, and only such opinions on the literary revolution as those of Mr. Liu and his contemporaries could be produced. Moreover, even if Mr. Liu had some non-thorough aspects, we cannot deny his achievements in the Chinese New Literature Movement because of this.

But now that Mr. Liu has passed away, apart from continuing the spirit of the May Fourth New Literature Movement and striving for a newer literary revolution, I am afraid we can only feel sorrow.

Agreement on Preventing Robbery of Postal Agency Businesses, "Pi Ju" and "Pi Yin" in Other Ports 321

— He Henchen

Correspondence from Chaozhou

"Pi Ye," here, don't think it refers to the job of a senior official, holding a vermilion pen and writing "Approved" and "As Requested," or the "fortune-telling" career of a Jianghu fortune teller. "Pi Ju" is also not the yamen of an official or a fortune-telling hall. And "Pi Yin," at first glance, seems to be a term in economics and finance, but if you want to find this term in books, you won't be able to find it even if you tear through all the books on economics and finance. Of course, their "Agreement on Preventing Robbery" is also inexplicable. These three terms actually come from the same business. This business is very peculiar, and I think most of the readers don't know much about it, right? Well then, let me explain it to you here: this is a regional phenomenon, and its origin is Chaozhou, Guangdong.

Speaking of Chaozhou, you will remember that it is the place where the great Tang Dynasty writer Han Yu served as a prefect. Because when Prefect Han was here, he wrote a "Memorial to the Crocodile," which I think everyone who has received an old education has read, and our Chaozhou is therefore associated with it in people's minds. But today, times are different. Feudal literature, people know that it must be overthrown. The "Memorial to the Crocodile" is no longer valued, and our Chaozhou is also forgotten, right? There are occasional mentions of it: that is when poor friends in Shanghai, unable to make a living, send their clothes to pawnshops to get money, and are ridiculed by the shop assistants; or when down-and-out scholars, who desperately want to save face, take a small amount of money to Wusong Road to buy used suits, and are treated harshly by the shop assistants, and thus resentfully remember that this is all thanks to the people of our Chaozhou, and secretly curse them. Apart from this, our Chaozhou is rarely able to enter people's memories.

Yes, our Chaozhou should not be able to enter people's memories. Because there are no concessions opened to foreigners here; no smooth roads built by foreigners; no large cinemas, dance halls, and department stores opened by foreigners to provide people with happiness and enjoyment in the so-called "commercial areas." Nor are there beautiful natural or artificial landscapes for people to escape the summer heat or recuperate. In addition, the land is small and barren, and there are no special products that are valued by people, so it is also appropriate.

But this refers to the whole country. If we talk about Guangdong, it also occupies a considerable position economically.

I said above that the land here is small and barren, with absolutely no products. Why does it occupy an economic position? It turns out that a large portion of its residents go out to make a living. In addition to the pawnshops and used clothing businesses mentioned above, which are opened in Shanghai and other ports in China, there are also many who travel overseas to Southeast Asia to make a living. Although no one has come out to conduct a detailed survey, there is no doubt that they account for a very high percentage of the population here. Although they only run small businesses, or even mostly work as beasts of burden for others, the price they get is ultimately slightly higher than in China. They are all so hardworking and thrifty, and send most of their meager income back here. Because there are so many people, combined, it becomes a major, large income in Guangdong Province. According to a survey three years ago, this income is about 100 million yuan per year.

We don't have banks here. There is another organization that handles this kind of remittance business. This organization is similar to a money shop. We call it "Pi Ye" here; its institution is called "Pi Ju"; and the remitted money is called "Pi Yin."

But this "Pi Ju" is still not located in our Chaozhou, but in Shantou, because Shantou's transportation is more convenient than here, and it is also closer.

The business method of this "Pi Ju" is as follows:

Each "Pi Ju" must have branches or liaison offices in various parts of Southeast Asia. If overseas Chinese want to send money back home, they only need to hand the money and letters to the "Pi Ju" (if they are regular customers or have someone to guarantee, they can also owe money, but they have to pay very high interest and have a time limit for repayment). The "Pi Ju" will then issue a receipt and the remitter's letters and, depending on the amount of business at that time, send them back to the general "Pi Ju" in Shantou several times a month for large amounts, and once a month for smaller amounts. The general "Pi Ju" hires many "road horses" - that is, staff who specialize in delivering letters and silver. Once they receive the letters, they prepare enough cash and use these "road horses" to send it to the recipient's address, and read and explain their family letters to them, obtain the recipient's reply, and hand it over to the general "Pi Ju" to send back to the remitter's branch "Pi Ju" to give to the remitter.

This method is very old, but because its procedures are very clear and convenient for both the remitter and the recipient, it is still very popular and common today. However, in the past few months, it has also inevitably been blown by the hurricane of the world's economic downturn, and is gradually declining.

Originally, the reason why overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, and even the entire overseas area, have been able to create a considerable historical position is due to the European War. At that time, all countries were busy with war, and drove the youth of production to the battlefield, so they had no time to take care of the rear. Our compatriots took the opportunity to advance and ran overseas to do production work for them, and thus multiplied. By the time the European War ended, and coupled with the capitalist countries "deceiving each other," an "economic downturn" was brewing, creating unprecedented unemployment. They themselves have no way to solve the unemployment problem, so how can they tolerate our overseas Chinese to share their food? As a result, many vicious conspiracies were created, new rejections and old expulsions were made against our overseas Chinese. Our overseas Chinese are unorganized and unprotected, so of course they cannot resist, and their livelihoods are suddenly reduced. This is the general reason for the decline of "Pi Ye."

I have explained twice above that Chaozhou is small and barren, so even if it wants to produce, it lacks raw materials. Therefore, young and strong men cannot gain a foothold in their homeland. Their only way out is to go to Southeast Asia. Now Southeast Asia is "a dead end." This cuts off their livelihood. The world's robbers and petty thieves are all forced to "take risks" because of the pressure of life. Naturally, the final actions of these unemployed youths are self-evident.

As a result, the "road horses" of the "Pi Ju" are often robbed. Two or three years ago, our Chaozhou had the beautiful environment I described above, and it was truly a peaceful and prosperous age. Therefore, although the "road horses" were carrying piercing things, no one dared to violate the "king's law" and "patronize" them. They could carry out their duties freely without weapons. This has been passed down from generation to generation and has almost become a habit. Unexpectedly, the situation suddenly changed, and they could not cope. At the most

Special Discussion

The Actual Tasks of Building Popular Language 322

— Ding Yi

I. Introduction

The issue of building a popular language has been discussed very enthusiastically, and several supplements' editors are sounding the retreat, as if they feel satisfied or tired of this discussion. In fact, as long as we pay attention to the opinions expressed by various people since the debate began, we will know that there is still no good conclusion so far. Everyone's opinions are still like blind people touching an elephant, thinking they have touched the whole thing when they have only touched a part. Moreover, no one has explained the basic understanding of this issue in detail. Therefore, even if I am as shallow as I am, I cannot help but join in the fun and offer some opinions.

II. Building a Popular Language is the Actual Demand of the Masses

"What is a popular language?" This is the question that most people first demand to be answered, and some people use this sentence as an excuse to oppose the popular language, just like when emerging literature was just emerging, celebrities and professors kept clamoring to "see the goods." Mr. Chen Zizhan, Chen Wangdao, and others believe that what can be heard, read, understood, and written is a popular language. Of course, there is nothing wrong with this, but it is not enough to explain the doubts of the general public. For example, someone asks: Isn't the popular vernacular written and understandable? Try to give an example of an article written in popular language - this will leave you speechless. At the current stage, our understanding of the popular language issue cannot be regarded as having a fixed form, but only as something that is developing due to the actual demands of the masses. In the face of the fierce attacks of imperialism and the panic of rural economic bankruptcy, the desperate war of the masses makes them urgently demand to create their own culture and even demand to build a linguistic form that expresses their lives. The popular language issue is not a simple linguistic issue, but is in line with the masses' anti-imperialist and anti-archaistic movements. Without the practice of the masses, the popular language cannot be established. "Take out the goods to see," if we start from such an understanding, we will know how ignorant and deceitful this sentence is. May I ask, when Mr. Sun Yat-sen first advocated the national revolution for the demands of the Chinese masses, could he take out any goods to see?

III. Is it Natural Development or Conscious Movement?

Some people regard the issue of building a popular language as a matter of natural language development. That's right, from vernacular language to popular language, it can be said that popular language is the upward development of vernacular language, just as capitalism develops from feudal society. Vernacular language itself contains elements of popular language. However, what cannot be forgotten here is that social evolution, in addition to the law of natural development, also has a kind of conscious movement. Society is progressing in contradiction at all times. When this contradiction expands to the point where it hinders its own progress, then a force is needed to push it forward. This push has the meaning of "anti." The current proposal to build a popular language is undoubtedly a conscious movement, undoubtedly because the vernacular language has been stolen by bureaucrats and compradors, and has lost its progressiveness. To advance it to the stage of popular language requires force, which requires not only a struggle against the classical language that attempts to revive, but also against the vernacular language that has lost its progressiveness. Peaceful development is enough to make the vernacular language surrender more and more to the classical language and foreign stereotyped writing. It is even more impossible to improve and correct it.

IV. Where to Start

Without the entire cultural movement and the practice of the masses, the popular language issue cannot be resolved. Then, how do we start building? This seems to have become a difficult hurdle. Mr. Hu Yuzhi advocates creating phonetic writing first, and Mr. Tao Xingzhi advocates educating the masses first. Mr. Hu's opinion can only be regarded as an ultimate goal of this movement. Putting it forward now does have the danger of canceling this movement, because a change in writing is by no means something that can be accomplished in a short time. It can never be said that we cannot talk about the popular language issue because there is no phonetic writing. If Mr. Tao regards education as education in the form of schools, it is not a good way. Mr. Tao's own educational experience has probably gained a lot of lessons. I think:

(1) As mentioned above, popular language is the actual

The present of building a popular language must first enrich the content of the masses' cultural struggle and strengthen the masses' anti-imperialist and anti-archaistic movement. Only with rich life content can a sound form of expressing this content be produced.

(2) Promoting the unification of language and writing from the development of local language and dialect literature will lead to the future of phonetic writing. Only in this way can this movement be combined with the actual lives of the masses in various places.

Page 22

When they first discovered that bandits would rob, they also carried pistols with them, but when they encountered bandits, they lost the method and courage to use the pistols. As a result, they would inevitably have both the silver and the pistols robbed. And the bandits, having robbed the pistols, would be even more "like a tiger with wings." This is also a clear reason for the decline of "Pi Ye."

"Pi Ye" has been greatly hit, so they are looking for remedies. The first reason is something they don't quite understand, and it is not something that their partial strength can solve. They have no choice but to try to salvage it from the second reason. Not long ago, they convened a guild and resolved this "Anti-Robbery Agreement."

The full text of this agreement is as follows:

(1) If "Pi Yin" is robbed on the road, the nearby villages must immediately come to the rescue. If they can capture the actual robber on the spot, and send him to the official for interrogation and conviction together with this guild, a reward of 200 silver dollars will be given by the guild for each actual robber captured.

(2) If "Pi Yin" is robbed on the road, the nearby villages must immediately come to the rescue. If they can capture the actual robber on the spot and recover the robbed "Pi Yin," in addition to implementing Article 1, the loser will withdraw 200 yuan from every 1,000 yuan of the recovered "Pi Yin" as a reward.

(3) If the villagers are injured by the robbers while coming to the rescue, those who are seriously injured will be given 5,000 yuan for medical expenses; those who are slightly injured will be rewarded appropriately; those who become disabled due to serious injuries will be given an additional reward of 200 silver dollars for post-care expenses.

(4) If the villagers are seriously injured and die while coming to the rescue, 500 silver dollars will be given as a consolation payment.

(5) The guild is not responsible for redeeming "road horses" who are kidnapped. If they are injured or killed as a result of being kidnapped, the guild will give an appropriate consolation payment.

(6) The rewards and consolations are the same whether on a ship or on land.

(7) If the nearby villages sit idly by and do not come to the rescue when a "road horse" is in danger, in addition to being reported to the official for investigation, the overseas "Pi Ju" will be notified to stop "Pi Yin" in that area.

This agreement is only a passive measure of "treating the head when it hurts" and "treating the feet when they hurt." In my opinion, the effectiveness of this passive measure is equal to zero, because the "actual robbers" are the "villages" who are expected to come to the rescue!

From this point, we can see the entire state of Chaozhou Society!

Scientific Miscellany

The Story of the Invention of the Airship (6) 325

— Shulin

The first six airships built by Zeppelin were all ruined and failed. The seventh one was 500 feet long, but it was still smashed to pieces by a storm.

Due to the frequent occurrence of accidents, various countries temporarily became indifferent to the matter of manufacturing airships. Especially after the start of World War I, various countries focused on the manufacture of airplanes, and paid even less attention to large airships.

Germany alone, in the midst of the neglect of various countries, achieved the large Zeppelin-style airship. It was more than 500 feet long and the whole body was divided into several small parts, each of which was equipped with a light gas bag. Even if one of them was destroyed by gun-cannon fire, the airship would not fall. The Zeppelin airship was rigid, and the entire skeleton was made of aluminum alloy, covered with linen cloth, and the internal balloon was made of cow intestine skin.

During the European War, Germany, surrounded by enemy forces on all sides, did not act with trepidation, but filled this monster with bombs, passed through the Allied army positions at night, crossed the Dover Strait, and leisurely attacked London, the capital of England, from afar. Not only did the people of London suffer from the harm of bombs, but also their hearts were greatly threatened.

Next, let's talk about Count Zeppelin. Zeppelin's life is a good model for displaying the German spirit.

IV. About Count Zeppelin

Ferdinand von Zeppelin, the inventor of the Zeppelin-style airship, was born on July 8, 1838, in the Count's family on the shore of Lake Constance. The count, with the temperament of a North German, was rich in will from an early age, lively and fond of traveling. It is said that he had a special interest in natural science from an early age.

After Zeppelin grew up, he entered the military academy and went to the United States as a German general. At that time, the American Civil War was just beginning. Once, Zeppelin and two or three colleagues went to visit the Niagara Falls. Zeppelin said:

"There is nothing interesting about looking at this waterfall on land. It is better to watch it while swimming." As he spoke, he jumped into the rapids regardless of his friends' dissuasion and swam to appreciate it. Although this matter is inevitably reckless, Zeppelin's spirit cannot but be admired here.

Soon after, he returned to Germany, and the Franco-Prussian War began. 850,000 German troops, due to the skillful operations of the famous general Mouge, invaded France, captured Napoleon III in Sedan, and besieged Paris, the capital. The citizens of Paris stubbornly resisted for four months, and finally opened the city and surrendered due to exhaustion.

This is the story of the siege of Paris.

Count Zeppelin also served in the army as a general. One day, he saw a balloon flying high in the sky in Paris. The balloon soared upwards and flew over the German army positions due to the wind, flowing towards the distant countryside. The soldiers below were solemnly guarding their positions, not knowing what to do, fearing that the balloon would communicate with the French army outside the city and transmit secret orders.

Zeppelin was greatly impressed by this balloon.

After this, Zeppelin buried himself in the research of airships. This fact was the motive.

Zeppelin was appointed Colonel for his merits in this war, then promoted to Major General, and then elected as a military adviser to participate in and interfere with political affairs. At the age of fifty-three, he retired and returned to the countryside.

After achieving success and fame, Mr. Qi did not, like ordinary people, enjoy his remaining years with romance and entertainment. At the old age of fifty-three, he attempted to invent an airship. (To be continued)

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

The Use of "Popular Language" in Film (Part 2) 326

— Danfeng

Generally speaking, a nation should preserve the existence of its different language forms; this cannot be equated with preserving each nation's inherent language and culture. The reason is simple: for the healthy development of a free and independent nation, its language should be completely unified to form a unified culture. If we want to maintain every different dialect or local vernacular, it would be tantamount to splitting national unity. Therefore, in film, we can produce purely Mongolian or Tibetan films, even Miao films, but we should never have Cantonese or Fujian films within the Han ethnicity.

Furthermore, we should strive to eliminate local dialects and vernaculars. In fact, when domestic transportation fully connects the cultures of various regions, local vernaculars will not exist forever, although it is still impossible to melt the national language into one. Therefore, we acknowledge that film is a tool of education, and unifying the languages of various regions through the language and text of film, helping to eliminate the existence of dialects and vernaculars, is a necessary task at present. Why should we advocate the use of dialects and vernaculars in film? Currently, we strongly oppose the production of sound films with Cantonese dialogue.

Regarding this point, we may as well give another example. We are, of course, absolutely opposed to classical Chinese subtitles in the style of "If Heaven does not rain, what shall we do?". On the other hand, we are equally opposed to such profound colloquial language as, "What shall we do? If the heavens are forever so stingy and unwilling to send down a drop of sweet rain." Furthermore, if we use our local dialect at home, it would be something like, "If this sky never rains, what are we all going to do?". Can this kind of popular language be understood by the general public? If it were translated into Cantonese or Fujianese, it would be even more incomprehensible. Therefore, the popular language suitable for film is, "It hasn't rained for days, what should we do?", a very clear and concise sentence.

I remember not long ago, someone in the local supplement of the Shen Bao used a whole section of Pudong or Ningbo dialect, "×倷×倷," as an example of popular language, which was clearly a malicious distortion. Popular language is not about promoting popular dialects and vernaculars, but about liberating language and writing from written vernacular and making it something that is easily understood by the public. Of course, there are many difficulties in this process, especially in practice. If we intellectuals are unwilling to delve into the masses and do not discover and create from actual life, we will not succeed.

As for the creation of films, in the current stage, we cannot yet unify the languages of various regions. In order to maintain local color, we may as well pay attention to the differences in pronunciation, just like the German music professor in "Little Women," who can have a German accent, and John Barrymore in "The Mad Genius," who can also have a slight Russian "R" accent. And for Jiangnan subjects, we can emphasize their local color in pronunciation, and the same is true for Shandong or Guangdong. This is not just a matter of acting skills; everyone engaged in the film culture movement should pay attention to this. (End)

Film Reviews

Review of "A Romantic Writer" 327

— Danfeng

Affairs of a Gentleman—Cathay—

Like most vulgar American films, this one does not lack love entanglements between men and women; what is different is that it also adds some of the elements unique to detective films.

The general story is like this: A writer has had romantic relationships with many women, and later, because of these entangled love affairs, he even tells his servant that he will commit suicide. So the servant says that even if he commits suicide, he must write a suicide note to the "Police" in his own handwriting to avoid implicating others. He does as his servant says, but in the end, he dies at the hands of his servant. The play begins with the death of the writer. The police find the suicide note and then, from a publisher's mouth, learn that the deceased had hosted many old lovers the night before. Thus, the story narrates the dinner party at the time and his difficulty in coping with the many women, resulting in an attempt to commit suicide after being repeatedly stimulated. Finally, the servant, seeing that he is not committing suicide but the suicide note is written, takes advantage of this opportunity, fueled by the old resentment that the master has committed adultery with his wife, and shoots the writer.

This work adopts the form of a detective film, but the main purpose is to write about the writer's entanglements with women. The playwright has achieved little else besides structuring the relationships between each character quite tightly. And to say that he is attacking writers for treating love as a trifle is simply echoing what others have said, feeling bored in meaningless entanglements. Comparatively, he used the same techniques as in plays, unfolding the characters tightly and explaining their conflicting contradictions. Therefore, those dialogues, if regarded as a play, are quite interesting. In the end, he tells us that the bougeoisie writer's life is so licentious, and the price is being shot by a lover's husband. However, the playwright has not fully depicted this aspect, if exposing them was the main point.

The director achieved the degree that the playwright wanted to describe, but the constant sitting and dialogue made the play exceptionally dull in the middle. This kind of play is not considered brilliant even in "business acumen."

From the story to the performance, from the set to the photography, there is nothing particularly commendable. Even every actor is, on the whole, very mediocre.

Evaluating the films of small companies is a more difficult task; this "Sacrifice for Whom?" produced by Jixing Company is no exception. Jixing Company's "Sacrifice for Whom?" is a film based on the theme of the Volunteer Army.

Movie Novel

20th Century Limited (Part 3) 331

— Wen Yin

The train started. Jifu curled up in the corner of the compartment, watching Chicago unfold outside the window scene by scene. Scattered under his feet were things like wide-brimmed glasses and fake beards. He sighed deeply and said to his two companions, "I never thought I would fall to this point and become an actor myself. This is really a shameful thing." O'Malley remembered the root of their failure, so he grinned and said, "It's a pity you didn't play "Joan of Arc" yourself." Jifu said, "Among the sixty-eight plays I've done, the most artistic one is "Joan of Arc." Alas, what a great failure! O'Malley, if I am a genius, I owe it to my failure. You must remember this clearly." Webb interjected solemnly, "Jifu, listen. We will arrive in New York at 9:45 tomorrow morning, and the bank opens at 10 o'clock. Three banks have your IOUs, totaling 221,000 yuan. The first thing they will do tomorrow morning is to run to your Jifu Theater and seal its doors... Then your fake beard will be useless!" After he finished speaking, he looked at Jifu sadly. Jifu jumped up and said, "They dare?" But he slumped back down, feeling a little scared in his heart. Webb then stuttered and said again, "Jifu, listen. There is still one way. If you can find a way to get Lilian Garland to sign a contract, then you don't have to be afraid of anything. Lilian Garland is also on this train now." Jifu couldn't help pressing his hand to his chest and said miserably, "Lilian... is she on the train?" O'Malley said, "Don't pretend. Her compartment is next door." Jifu smiled and said, "I think maybe she did it on purpose." O'Malley said, "I also think she did it on purpose." Jifu sat up straight and said, "Since she came here, she has already made the first move. It's my turn to make the second move. I would rather meet her halfway." O'Malley said, "Great. As long as you can get her to sign the contract, then all our worries can be turned into nothing. But I can't help but think that it's probably not an easy task." Jifu said very easily, "In fact, there is no break between us." O'Malley, you can send a telegram to the flower shop in Toledo and ask them to send all the good flowers to..." O'Malley continued, "Compartment B." Jifu continued, "Okay, Compartment B of this train... And that note... Let me see... O'Malley, get a pencil. I think this is how it should be written..." He paused for a moment, then recited with emotion, "From the tomb of someone you loved yesterday!" He lay back down, closed his eyes, and savored the taste of those words. Then he sighed and said, "These words are really perfect, nothing could be more appropriate. Why don't I read a few books when I have this kind of talent?" O'Malley silently wrote down the note. He never dared to say anything when Jifu was happy. Jifu said to him again, "O'Malley, I want you to go and meet her first, like a chance encounter. You can casually mention that I have already written a script for her. Ah, going up to meet her like this can be said to be a sure thing. You can open that briefcase, which is full of scripts. They are all wonderful works." O'Malley glanced at him, then pretended to be helpless and said, "Are you going to do that again?" Jifu quickly comforted him, "Don't worry. You just need to tell her that I have found a good script for her. She can play a person who is half devil and half woman, who made a great sacrifice for love. Okay. Okay. Go!" He stood up and pushed him towards the door. (To be continued)
